As an Amazon Prime member, I was able to buy the Fire TV Stick for $19 during a two day sale.  I figured, for that price, I might as well test it out!<br /><br />Set up was easy and straight forward.  I find that the interface is quick and easy to use.  The interface and streaming on the Stick is much faster than the Amazon app built into my HDTV.  This fact alone made this a great purchase. Here are some more thoughts I have on the Fire TV Stick so far:<br /><br />&#10004; PROS:<br /><br />- Quick, easy to use, polished interface<br />- Wireless streaming works really well<br />- Amazon Instant video loads, fast forwards, and rewinds really fast<br />- A dedicated Prime Menu allows Prime members to easily see what free content is available<br />- Unlike Chromecast, the Fire TV Stick includes a remote<br />- Can stream your own videos by first uploading them to your cloud disk<br />- Can play quite a few casual games<br />- Awesome, irresistible price for Amazon Prime users. I got it for $19 during the two day sale.<br />- Better specs than Chromecast and Roku Stick<br />- Ultraportable.  I plan to use Fire TV Stick when I travel for work and to visit family<br />- Stream local videos and other content using the Plex app http://www.amazon.com/Plex-Inc/dp/B004Y1WCDE/ (Thanks BikeRider!)<br /><br />&#10004; CONS:<br /><br />- Included remote doesn't support voice search.  That remote costs extra.  Would be nice to have a second Fire TV Stick model that includes the voice search remote, rather can requiring us to buy a second remote.<br />- Probably won't be able to use universal remotes with this unless Logitech offers a compatible device.<br />- Not as fast as Fire TV, but since the Stick is so much cheaper, this is not really an issue.</span><span class="MHRRest" style="display:none"><br />- Limited compatibility with older Android devices.<br /><br />&#10004; OTHER<br /><br />- Arrived associated with my Amazon account.  You can change this of course.  Just keep this in mind if you are sending the Fire TV Stick as a gift.<br /><br />- Unlike the Chromecast, the Fire TV Stick may complain if you connect its power port to a USB port on your TV instead of using the included AC power brick.<br /><br />- Setup will take 15 to 20 minutes<br /><br />- Would be nice if this thing was compatible with the Fire Keyboard: http://www.amazon.com/review/R1DFOMPMA8NG4V/<br /><br />&#10004; AMAZON FIRE TV STICK vs CHROMECAST<br /><br />Chromecast is cheaper these days.  It's a very capable device. It currently has a few notable content sources that Fire TV Stick doesn't have, including HBO Go and Sling Player.  It doesn't have a remote and I find the user interface to be a little clunky.<br /><br />Amazon Fire TV Stick has a remote and a very quick and easy to use interface.  Your non-technically inclined family members will find the Fire TV Stick easier to use than the Chromecast.  If you have Amazon Prime, it's a no brainer.  Chose the Stick over the Chromecast.<br /><br />&#10004; AMAZON FIRE TV STICK vs FIRE TV<br /><br />The Fire TV is faster, includes voice search, has more RAM, has more storage, has an Ethernet port, and can play more games.  It's also more expensive (although there are discounts on them all the time).<br /><br />The Fire TV Stick is more portable.  It's also a lot cheaper, especially if you are an Amazon Prime member and got the initial $19 price.<br /><br />If you can afford to the Fire TV, get that.  Otherwise the Fire TV Stick is a great alternative.  I plan to own both. :-)<br /><br />&#10004; BOTTOM LINE<br /><br />I really like the Amazon Fire TV Stick.  At only $19 for Amazon Prime members (during the 2 day sale), I REALLY, REALLY LIKE Fire TV Stick.<br />Its interface is faster and easier to use than my HDTV's built-in Amazon app, plus it includes a lot more video sources.  It's really the best way to view your Amazon content on a TV.<br /><br />The interesting thing is, Fire TV Stick has convinced me to buy the more expensive Fire TV too.  I want to have the voice search and the faster interface on my main HDTV.  I plan to take the Fire Stick with me when I travel for work or travel to visit family.<br /><br />For Amazon Prime members, and for anyone that has a few Amazon movie/TV purchases, the both the Fire TV and the Fire TV Stick are must have devices and great stocking stuffers for this Christmas.<br /><br />*** If you like this review, please mark this review as helpful! reviewTitle valignMiddle"><strong>Best streamer for your dollar - from a roku & firetv box user</strong></a><span class="gry valignMiddle">        <span class="inlineblock txtsmall">November 20, 2014</span> </span></div>  <div class="mt4 ath"><span class="gr10">        <span class="txtsmall"><span class="gry">By</span> <a href="/gp/pdp/profile/A1UIMU8Q87ZPCH/ref=cm_cr_dp_pdp/187-9325419-6173254" class="noTextDecoration">Darren Levine</a></span> </span>   </div>  <div class="mt9 reviewText">       <div class="drkgry">   <span class="MHRHead">Bottom line? This is the best streaming device for the dollar(In my humble opinion) Keep in mind... it's $39 & it handles netflix/prime/plex/games and a lot more. Thus far it's been a smooth operating device & doesn't seem that much slower than the full firetv box<br /><br />***TIP!:<br />Some have mentioned that their stick's usb port gets obstructed, there's an easy fix: just search amazon for "HDMI Angle"<br /><br />I've been using the firetv box right from the start, and it's been overall very nice for my living room. I've also used the roku 2 for quite some time, and have few complaints overall. For my bedroom i wanted something that just plugs in, and i tried the roku stick but returned it because it was just too darn slow. When i saw the specs on this amazon stick, i ordered up pretty darn quick.<br /><br />The Good stuff...<br /><br />-Same pricerange as the less capable/less powered Chromecast & Roku stick<br />-More ram/memory than the competition, keeps things running smooth<br />-More storage space than the competition, you can store more apps/games/etc..<br />-You can still do gaming with it, but the firetv box is better suited<br />-So small you can bring it pretty much anywhere with ease.<br />-Simple clean interface.<br />-Lots of games/apps to choose from<br />-The phone app is actually pretty useful<br /><br />Not as good stuff...<br /><br />-No connections other than usb for power, if you need ethernet/audio in/out, get the box!<br />-STILL no HBO go... what's going on amazon?<br />-Not nearly as much power as the firetv box, but it's also less than half the price, the power difference is not very apparent in general use.<br />-No voice search without the additional remote(or phone app), but i really never used it<br /><br />Plex...</span><span class="MHRRest" style="display:none"><br />So far, seems to work without much delay on my fairly speedy home network. will update if i run into lag/issues.<br /><br />Wireless connectivity quality...<br />I use it in a room that's next to the wireless router room, and it gives a solid signal. At some point i'll try to do a distance test.<br /><br />Should you get this, firetv box, roku, or chromecast?<br />Roku has been fine for me, but if we're talking about something cleaner/no wires/direct plugin/etc... then there's not much contest, the roku stick was too slow for me, and an android stick isn't as clean to use, so to speak. That leaves chromecast, which i've never used because i don't like having to rely on a computer/device for it to work, i want what i plug in to be able to handle the task. Needless to say, the stick in my view has not much competition.<br /><br />Vs Firetv box<br />If i were to be shown the experience side by side with the firetv box, i'd have a hard time knowing any difference in most cases, so which should you get considering the more than 2x higher price for the box?<br /><br />If you don't need extra connections like audio and ethernet, and don't plan on using voice search(the stick remote lacks it, but i never used it anyways, as it only searching prime) and don't plan on heavy gaming,  then absolutely get the stick, it's been a solid experience thus far.<br /><br />______________<br /><br />Side note... it seems amazon is putting up other types of apps, like a digital fireplace/rain storm/sunset/etc... Not that it's amazing, but interesting additions to add to the checklist of this items abilities.</span> <a people found the following review helpful</div>  <div class="clearboth"></div>  <div class="mt4 ttl"><span class="swSprite s_star_5_0 " title="5.0 out of 5 stars" ><span>5.0 out of 5 stars</span></span>   <a href="http://www.amazon.com/review/R25DZSLY6Q1RE/ref=cm_cr_dp_title/187-9325419-6173254?ie=UTF8&ASIN=B00GDQ0RMG&nodeID=3213029011&store=daisy-store" class="txtlarge gl3 gr4 reviewTitle valignMiddle"><strong>This thing is awesome!  Here's why you need it.</strong></a><span class="gry valignMiddle">        <span class="inlineblock txtsmall">November 20, 2014</span> </span></div>  <div class="mt4 ath"><span class="gr10">        <span class="txtsmall"><span class="gry">By</span> <a href="/gp/pdp/profile/AZKRFNQ8EFO4T/ref=cm_cr_dp_pdp/187-9325419-6173254" class="noTextDecoration">Mike Williams</a></span> </span>   </div>  <div class="txtsmall mt4 fvavp"><span class="inlineblock avpOrVine" ><span class="orange strong avp">Verified Purchase</span></span></div>  <div class="mt9 reviewText">       <div class="drkgry">   <span class="MHRHead">Since the Fire TV stick was announced, I've heard a lot of people wonder if it was something worth picking up, essentially asking "what does this thing do that my TV doesn't do already?"  The answer is going to be different for different people, but here's an easy way to think about it; Amazon Fire TV Stick is an excellent purchase if:<br /><br />-Your TV is not a "smart" TV.  Meaning your TV or dvd player did not come pre-loaded with apps such as Netflix, Youtube, Pandora etc...<br /><br />-Your TV is a "smart" TV, but apps do not perform well.  Some smart TVs have painful performance when streaming video, apps can be difficult to update, wifi connection can be spotty etc...<br /><br />-You want to access Youtube, Netflix, Amazon Prime, Pandora, and other such apps on your TV<br /><br />-You are an Amazon Prime Member and want to access your Prime Video, Prime Music, and Prime Photo accounts<br /><br />-You want to participate in casual gaming on your television.<br /><br />-You want to listen to music on your TV<br /><br />-You want to have portability.  In other words, Television access to the above services while you are travelling. (Amazon says the capability to use in hotels/dorms etc... with shared wifi that requires frequent password entry is coming soon)<br /><br />So, the bottom line is that the Fire TV Stick allows you to access your movies, music and photos as well as games and more  via your television.  If your TV already does these things well, or you're already doing them via other devices such as a game console, then this may not be worth your while.<br /><br />So, how easy is it to use?  I'm telling you, you do not have to have an ounce of technological know how to have this thing up and running in a matter of minutes.</span><span class="MHRRest" style="display:none"> There is a set of 5 very simple instructions for set-up that had me watching House of Cards less than 10 minutes after I unboxed it.  It comes with a remote that includes just 7 buttons  (your phone can also become a remote by adding an app, though this is not quite ready on the iPhone yet) and upon completion of connecting the stick, you are taken to a simple tutorial video that explains very well the use of the remote.  There is also an optional voice control remote that can be separately purchased.  It is in no way required to operate the Fire Stick.  Sidenote:  If you buy the Stick online, it comes preset to the account from which it is ordered.  If this is not the account you plan to use (I needed to use my wife's because she has the prime account) it's very easy de-register and change accounts; took me less than a minute.<br /><br />I have accessed Prime Video and the picture and speed is fantastic.  I've accessed Prime Music and the sound quality and speed are excellent and include nice background photos of artists and albums.  Apps are easy to browse and download as are games.  I was also able to "fling" to Netflix etc... from my Kindle Fire quite easily.<br /><br />I've been using a Chromecast since they came out, and I think the Fire TV Stick competes very well.  I like the remote (which the Chromecast doesn't have), and I love the memory and speed.  And if you are an Amazon Prime Member, this is hands down your best option. This would make a great gift, and is easy enough to use that you could give it with confidence to someone who has no technological savvy at all.<br /><br />If you're looking to get the most out of your HDTV, The Fire Stick is a fantastic way to go about it.  I highly recommend it, and based on how smoothly everything went on what was probably a very busy day for Amazon servers, I'm confident that you'll have the same or an even better experience.  Enjoy!</span> <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Amazon-W87CUN-Fire-TV-Stick/product-reviews/B00GDQ0RMG/ref=cm_cr_dp_text/187-9325419-6173254?ie=UTF8&showViewpoints=0&sortBy=byRankDescending#R25DZSLY6Q1RE"
